Exception of Non-Homogeneous Items from Dirhams: Istihsan vs Qiyas
Ruling on exception of different genus and the istihsan debate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf validate the exception of a cubic/weight item from a debt of dirhams by istihsan, distinguish this from Muhammad's qiyas position, and derive the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf).

Core Idea
Exception of a different type is valid if both are price-commeasurable, by istihsan overriding qiyas.

This passage presents a key intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute over the validity of excluding a different type of property (like a dinar) from an acknowledgment of dirhams. The matn states the ruling: if the excepted item is cubic or weight, it is valid; otherwise not. The commentator then explains the reasoning: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf use istihsan based on the common function as price, while Muhammad and others adhere to strict qiyas. Understanding this dispute clarifies how Hanafi usul operates when istihsan overrides analogy.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling and its conditions
Identify the ruling from the matn: exception of a cubic or weight measure from dirhams is valid; exception of other types is invalid. Note the condition that the excepted item must be makil (cubic) or mawzun (weight).
The matn also distinguishes between same wording and different wording, but the core dispute is about genus.
2
Identify the basis of the Hanafi position
The commentator states it is istihsan: all items that serve as price (thaman) in the dhimma are considered one genus in meaning, even if physically different. This justifies the exception.
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf adopt this view.
3
Present the opposing qiyas argument
Muhammad al-Shaybani, Zufar, and Ahmad ibn Hanbal argue by qiyas: exception requires the excepted item to be included in the original statement; a different genus cannot be included, so the exception is invalid.
This is the stricter analogical reasoning.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response uses istihsan: despite physical difference, the shared function as price creates a meaningful similarity, overriding qiyas to avoid hardship and reflect custom.
Istihsan is a legitimate source in the Hanafi school.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
In practice, under Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf, the debtor pays the original amount minus the value of the excepted item. Under Muhammad, the debtor pays the full original amount because the exception is invalid.
This practical difference is the thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن استثنى كيلياً أو وزنيّاً من دراهم صح قيمته، وإن استثنى غيرهما منها لم يصح (فإن استثنى كيلياً أو وزنيّاً من دراهم صح قيمته، وإن استثنى غيرهما منها لم يصح)، إن قال له: علي مئة درهم إلا ديناراً، وإلا قفيز حنطة صح الاستثناء، وإن قال: إلا ثوباً لم يصح، هذا عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف؛ لوجود المجانسة من وجه إذا كان مكيلاً أو موزوناً، وعند محمد: لا يصح في الكل لعدم المجانسة، وعند الشَّافِعِي: يصح في الكل للمجانسة من حيث المالية به، فيكون رجوعاً، فلا يصح، وهذا إذا استثنى بعين اللفظ الذي تكلم به في صدر الكلام بأن قال: علي عشرة إلا عشرة أو قال: هؤلاء أحرار إلا هؤلاء. أما إذا كان بخلاف لفظ المستثنى منه، بأن يقول: عبيدي أحرار إلا هؤلاء، أو نسائي طوالق إلا هؤلاء، أو عبيدي أحرار إلا مباركاً وسالماً وبريقاً، أو نسائي طوالق إلا زينب وخالدة وهند، وليس له عبيد ولا نساء غير المستثنى منه، صح الاستثناء فلا يعتق واحد منهم، ولا يطلق واحدة منهن؛ لأنه إذا اختلف اللفظ يتوهم بقاء شيء من المستثنى منه، إذ اللفظ صالح له، وذلك يكفي لصحة الاستثناء. كما صرحوا به. والفقه فيه: إنّ الاستثناء تصرف لفظي، فيبتني عليه صحة اللفظ لا على صحة الحكم). [1] قوله: إن قال له...الخ؛ يعني لو قال: له عليَّ مئة درهم إلا ديناراً، أو قال: له علي مئة درهم إلا قفيز حنطة، صح الاستثناء فيلزمه ألف درهم إلا قيمة القفيز من الحنطة أو الدينار، وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف، وهو الاستحسان. وقال محمد وزفر وأحمد: لا يصح هذا الاستثناء، وهو القياس؛ لأن الاستثناء إخراج بعض ما يتناوله صدر الكلام على معنى أنه لولا الاستثناء لكان داخلاً تحت الصدر، وهذا لا يتصور في خلاف الجنس. ووجه الاستحسان: إن المقدرات جنس واحد معنى، وإن كانت أجناساً صورة؛ لأنها تثبت في الذمة ثمناً، أما الدينار فظاهر، وكذا غيره؛ لأن الكيلي أو الوزني مبيع
If he excludes a cubic or weight measure from dirhams, its value is valid, and if he excludes other than them, it is not valid. So if he says: 'I owe him one hundred dirhams except a dinar, or except a qafiz of wheat,' the exception is valid, and if he says 'except a garment,' it is not valid. This is with Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf due to the existence of similarity in one respect if it is cubic or weight. And according to Muhammad, it is not valid in all due to lack of similarity. And according to al-Shafi'i, it is valid in all due to similarity from the perspective of value; [then] by it it would be a retraction, so it is not valid. This is if he excludes with the same wording as the first part of the speech, like saying 'I owe ten except ten' or 'these are free except these.' But if it is different wording from the object of exception, like saying 'my slaves are free except these,' or 'my wives are divorced except these,' or 'my slaves are free except Mubarak, Salim, and Burayq,' or 'my wives are divorced except Zaynab, Khalidah, and Hind,' and he has no slaves or wives other than the excluded ones, the exception is valid, so none of them are freed or divorced because if the wording differs, there is a possibility that something of the object of exception remains, as the wording is suitable for it, and that is sufficient for the validity of the exception, as they explicitly stated. And the fiqh of it: Exception is a verbal disposition, so its validity is based on the validity of the wording, not on the validity of the ruling. [1] His statement: 'If he says...' means: if he says 'I owe him one hundred dirhams except a dinar' or 'I owe him one hundred dirhams except a qafiz of wheat,' the exception is valid, so he is liable for one hundred dirhams minus the value of the qafiz of wheat or the dinar. This is with Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and it is istihsan. And Muhammad, Zufar, and Ahmad said: this exception is not valid, and it is qiyas, because the exception is the removal of some of what the first part of the speech encompasses, in the sense that if not for the exception it would be included in the first part, and this is not conceivable with a different genus. And the justification of istihsan: the measured things are one genus in meaning, even if they are different genus in form, because they are established in the dhimma as price. As for the dinar, it is obvious, similarly others because the cubic or weight is a [sale good].
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage presents a dispute regarding exception of a different type of property from an acknowledgment of dirhams. The matn states: if someone acknowledges a debt of dirhams and then makes an exception of something that is measured by weight or volume (like a dinar or a measure of wheat), the exception is valid at Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, and the debtor is liable for the dirhams minus the value of the excepted item. But if he excepts something not measurable, like a specific garment, the exception is invalid. The commentator explains that this ruling is based on istihsan, departing from strict qiyas. By qiyas, Muhammad al-Shaybani, Zufar, and Ahmad ibn Hanbal argue that since the excepted item is of a different genus (dinar vs. dirham), it cannot be considered part of the original acknowledgment, so the exception is invalid. The Hanafi istihsan view considers all things that serve as price (thaman) in the dhimma as one genus in meaning, despite different physical forms. This is because they are all established in the liability as value. The Shafi'i position is also mentioned: he would allow exception of anything based on commonality in value, but the commentator adds a note that this would make the exception a retraction (ruju') and thus invalid—though this may reflect a Hanafi criticism. The passage also clarifies that if the wording of the exception differs from the object (e.g., 'my slaves are free except these'), the exception can be valid even if there are no other slaves, due to the possibility that the wording could refer to others. This demonstrates that exception is a verbal disposition; its validity depends on the wording, not on the existence of the object.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Preferring a ruling that is more equitable over a strict analogy (qiyas) based on a stronger evidence or custom.
مكيل (makil): A commodity measured by volume (e.g., wheat).
موزون (mawzun): A commodity measured by weight (e.g., silver).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), if someone says 'I owe you 100 dirhams except a dinar,' what is the ruling?
A) The exception is invalid; he must pay 100 dirhams.
B) The exception is valid; he pays 100 dirhams minus the value of the dinar.
C) The exception is valid only if the dinar is mentioned after a pause.
D) The exception is invalid because the dinar is not of the same genus.

Key Takeaway
By istihsan, exception of cubic/weight items from dirhams is valid because both serve as price in the dhimma, overriding the qiyas requirement of genus identity.

Exception of Measured/Weighed Items from a Debt in Confession: Hanafi Position and Inter-Madhhab Dispute
Ruling on excepting kili/wazni from dirhams with ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on excepting kili/wazni items from a dirham debt, distinguish it from the positions of Muhammad, al-Shafi'i, and Malik, and apply the Hanafi view to practical confession scenarios.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, excepting a measured/weighed item from a dirham debt is valid by istihsan due to partial genus unity, while other items are not.

This passage addresses a common scenario in legal confessions: someone admits owing dirhams but then makes an exception of a different type of item. The Hanafi school, through istihsan, carves out a special rule for items that are measured or weighed because they share a functional genus as prices. We will examine the intra-Hanafi split and the cross-madhhab disagreement, then see how wording affects the exception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
The act is making an exception (istithnā') in a confession (iqrār) of debt. The ruling depends on the type of excepted item. Note the key terms: kīlī (measured) and waznī (weighed).
2
State the Hanafi position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, if the excepted item is measured or weighed (e.g., dinar, wheat), the exception is valid by istihsan. If it is something else (e.g., a garment), it is invalid.
This is based on partial genus unity (mujānasa min wajh): both dirhams and kili/wazni items serve as prices.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad and Zufar hold that the exception is invalid in all cases by qiyas, because there is no complete genus unity. The muftā bihi is the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
4
Present the opposing school view (Shafi'i/Maliki)
Al-Shafi'i and Malik hold that all exceptions are valid by mu'āraḍa (contradiction): the exception is a contradictory statement that negates the obligation for the excepted part, and its value must be deducted.
They consider homogeneity in monetary value sufficient.
5
Analyze the Hanafi response to mu'āraḍa
The Hanafi response refutes mu'āraḍa: contradiction requires the same subject (confession is a report that cannot be contradicted by denial). The Quranic example (29:14) shows exception of the same genus (years from years), not different genera.
Also, if mu'āraḍa were valid, it would apply equally to partial and total exceptions, which is not the case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن استثنى كيلياً أو وزنيّاً من دراهم صح قيمته ، وإن استثنى غيرهما منها لم يصح (فإن استثنى كيلياً أو وزنيّاً من دراهم صح قيمته ، وإن استثنى غيرهما منها لم يصح)، إن قال له : علي مئة درهم إلا ديناراً، وإلا قفير حنطة صح الاستثناء، وإن قال : إلا ثوباً لم يصح، هذا عند أبي حنيفة له وأبي يوسف له ؛ لوجود المجانسة من وجه إذا كان مكيلاً أو موزوناً ، وعند محمد ه : لا يصح في الكل لعدم المجانسة ، وعند الشَّافِعِي : يصح في الكل للمجانسة من حيث المالية به، فيكون رجوعاً، فلا يصح، وهذا إذا استثنى بعين اللفظ الذي تكلم به في صدرِ الكلام بأن قال: علي عشرة إلا عشرة أو قال : هؤلاء أحرار إلا هؤلاء. أما إذا كان بخلاف لفظ المستثنى منه ، بأن يقول : عبيدي أحرار إلا هؤلاء، أو نسائي طوالق إلا هؤلاء، أو عبيدي أحرار إلا مباركاً وسالماً وبريقاً، أو نسائي طوالق إلا زينب وخالدة وهند، وليس له عبيد ولا نساء غير المستثنى منه ، صح الاستثناء فلا يعتق واحد منهم، ولا يطلق واحدة منهن ؛ لأنه إذا اختلف اللفظ يتوهم بقاء شيء من المستثنى منه ، إذ اللفظ صالح له، وذلك يكفي لصحة الاستثناء. كما صرحوا به. والفقه فيه : إنّ الاستثناء تصرف لفظي، فيبتني عليه صحةُ اللّفظِ لا على صحة الحكم. بأعيانهما ثمن بأوصافهما، حتى لو عينا تعلق العقد بأعيانهما. ولو وصفا ولم يُعيّنا صار حكمها كحكم الثمنين؛ ولهذا يستوي الجيد والرديء فيهما، فكانت في حكم الثبوت في الذمة كجنس واحد معنى، فالاستثناء تكلم بالباقي معنى لا صورة، بخلاف غيرهما من الثوب وغيره، فإنه مثلاً ليس جنس المقدرات معنى؛ لأنه لا يصلح ثمناً، فلم يكن استثناؤه استخراجاً لا صورة ولا معنى، فكان باطلا معنى. وقال الشافعي: صح هذا الاستثناء، وبه قال مالك؛ لأن حكم الاستثناء امتناع ثبوت الحكم في المستثنى؛ لقيام الدليل المعارض، فإذا قال: له علي عشرة إلا خمسة، فكأنه قال: إلا خمسة فإنها ليست علي، فإذا كان بطريق المعارضة من جنسه يجب إخراج قدره، وإن كان من خلاف جنسه يجب إخراج قيمته عملا بالدليل المعارض بقدر الإمكان. والجواب: إن المعارضة لا تثبت عند اختلاف المحل؛ لأن انتفاء أحدهما لا ينافي ثبوت الآخر، فلا يتعارضان وأيضاً: إن العبد لا يقدر على أن ينفي ما عليه من الواجب بطريق المعارضة، فإنه إذا أقر به لزمه، ولا يتصور أن ينتفي بعد ذلك بإنكاره، ولو كان بطريق المعارضة كما ذكره؛ لاستوى فيه البعض والكل كما في النسخ والاتصال والانفصال؛ لأنه لا يشترط في المعارض أن يكون مقارناً، وإنما ذلك في المغير. وأيضاً: الإقرار خبر، فلو كان بطريق المعارضة لكان أحدهما كذباً، وذلك لا يجوز؛ لكونه موجوداً في القرآن المجيد، حيث قال عز من قال: فَلَبِثَ فِيهِمْ أَلْفَ سَنَةٍ إِلَّا خمسين عاما، والمراد به أنه لبث فيهم تسعمئة وخمسين عاما. وإن استثنى غير الكيلي والوزني من الدراهم لم يصح الاستثناء باتفاق أصحابنا، فإذا قال: له علي مئة درهم إلا ثوباً أو داراً أو شاة بطل الاستثناء اتفاقاً، ويلزمه مئة درهم؛ لأن ذلك القدر لا يفيد الاتحاد الجنسي، وعند الشافعي يطرح قيمته من المستثنى منه.
If he excepted a measured or weighed item from dirhams, its value is valid; if he excepted something else from them, it is not valid. If he said to him: I owe a hundred dirhams except a dinar, or except a qafiz of wheat, the exception is valid; if he said except a garment, it is not valid. This according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, due to partial homogeneity when it is measured or weighed. According to Muhammad: it is not valid in all cases due to lack of homogeneity. And according to al-Shafi'i: it is valid in all cases due to homogeneity in terms of monetary value, so it becomes a retraction and thus invalid? (incomplete) This if he excepted with the exact wording used in the first part of the speech, such as saying: I owe ten except ten, or saying: these are free except these. But if the wording differs from the excepted-from, such as saying: my slaves are free except these, or my women are divorced except these, or my slaves are free except Mubarak, Salim, and Burayq, or my women are divorced except Zaynab, Khalida, and Hind, and he has no other slaves or women other than the excepted ones, then the exception is valid, so none of them are freed nor any of them divorced, because when the wording differs, the possibility of something remaining from the excepted-from is imagined, as the wording is suitable for that, and that suffices for the validity of the exception, as they have clearly stated. And the juristic reasoning therein: the exception is a verbal act, so it is based on the validity of the wording, not on the validity of the ruling. By their entities they are price with their descriptions, so if they are specified, the contract attaches to their entities; if described but not specified, their ruling becomes like the ruling of two prices; hence the good and bad are equal in them, so they are in the ruling of being established in the dhimmah as a single genus in meaning, so the exception speaks of the remaining in meaning not in form, unlike other things like a garment and so on, for it is not a genus of measured items in meaning, because it is not suitable as a price, so its exception is not an extraction in form nor meaning, thus it is invalid in meaning. Al-Shafi'i said: This exception is valid, and Malik agreed, because the ruling of the exception is the prevention of establishing the ruling on the excepted due to a contradictory evidence. So if he says: I owe ten except five, it is as if he said: except five they are not owed by me. So if it is by way of contradiction from the same genus, its amount must be removed; if from a different genus, its value must be removed, acting on the contradictory evidence as much as possible. The answer: contradiction is not established when the subject differs, because the negation of one does not preclude the affirmation of the other, so they do not contradict. Also, the slave cannot deny what is obligatory upon him by way of contradiction, because if he confesses to it, it becomes binding, and it cannot be imagined to be negated afterwards by his denial. If it were by way of contradiction as he mentioned, then the partial and the whole would be equal, as in abrogation, connection and disconnection, because the contradictory is not required to be concurrent; rather that is in the modifier. Also, the confession is a report; if it were by way of contradiction, one of them would be a lie, and that is not permissible because it appears in the Noble Quran: 'Then he remained among them a thousand years except fifty years' (29:14), meaning he remained among them nine hundred and fifty years. And if he excepts something other than measured or weighed from dirhams, the exception is not valid by consensus of our scholars. So if he says: I owe a hundred dirhams except a garment, or a house, or a sheep, the exception is void by consensus, and he is liable for a hundred dirhams, because that amount does not effect genus unity; and according to al-Shafi'i, its value is deducted from the excepted-from.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and inter-madhhab dispute concerning the validity of making an exception (istithnā') in a debt confession (iqrār) when the excepted item is of a different type than the confessed amount. The Hanafi position, held by Imam Abū Ḥanīfa and Imam Abū Yūsuf, distinguishes between items that are measured (kīlī) or weighed (waznī) and other items. If someone says 'I owe 100 dirhams except a dinar' or 'except a qafīz of wheat', the exception is valid, and the debtor owes the dirhams minus the value of the dinar or wheat. This is based on istiḥsān (juristic preference), because measured and weighed items are considered a single genus in meaning—they can serve as price in a contract—even if different in form. Imām Muḥammad and Zufar disagree, applying qiyās (analogy): the exception must exclude part of what is covered by the initial statement; a different genus cannot be part of that, so the exception is invalid. Al-Shāfi'ī and Mālik hold a third view: all exceptions are valid because the commonality is monetary value; the exception functions as a contradiction (mu'āraḍa) to the initial claim, so the value of the excepted item must be subtracted. The Hanafi response refutes this by arguing that contradiction requires the same subject; confession is a report that once affirmed cannot be contradicted by denial; the Quranic example of 'a thousand years except fifty' (Q29:14) shows exception in the same category, not different. The passage also addresses wording: if the exception uses different wording than the initial statement (e.g., 'my slaves are free except these' where 'these' differs from 'slaves'), the exception is valid and none are freed because the possibility of remaining individuals is imagined. Finally, by consensus of the Ḥanafīs, excepting non-measured/weighed items (like a garment, house, or sheep) from dirhams is invalid, and the full 100 dirhams are owed.

Key Terms
استثناء (istithnā'): Exception; excluding a part from the generality of a statement in confession.
إقرار (iqrār): Confession; an admission of a right or debt.
كيلي (kīlī): An item measured by volume or capacity (e.g., wheat).
موزون (mawzūn): An item weighed (e.g., silver, gold).
المجانسة (al-mujānasa): Homogeneity or genus unity between the excepted and excepted-from.
المعارضة (al-mu'āraḍa): Contradiction; a proof that opposes another proof.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone confesses owing 100 dirhams but says 'except a garment', what is the ruling?
A) The exception is valid and the value of the garment is deducted.
B) The exception is invalid and the full 100 dirhams are owed.
C) The exception is valid if the garment is measured or weighed.
D) The confession is invalid.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits exception of measured/weighed items from a dirham debt by istihsan, rejecting the qiyas-based and mu'arada-based views.

6 min
Effect of Saying 'Insha'Allah' on a Confession
Ruling on attaching 'insha'Allah' to a confession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on a confession attached with 'insha'Allah' and explain why the phrase does not suspend the obligation.

Core Idea
Saying 'insha'Allah' does not suspend a binding confession; it is a blessing phrase, not a condition.

In legal practice, a person may qualify a confession with the phrase 'insha'Allah' (if Allah wills). Does this make the confession conditional or void? The Hanafi school addresses this question, affirming that the confession remains valid and enforceable because the phrase is understood as a blessing, not a suspending condition.

Guided Path
1
State the factual scenario
A person confesses a debt (e.g., 'I owe you 100 dirhams') and immediately adds 'insha'Allah' consecutively. The phrase is attached without a break.
The phrase must be connected (muttasil) for this ruling.
2
Identify the Hanafi position
The confession is valid and binding; the addition of 'insha'Allah' does not affect its enforceability. The debtor must fulfill the confessed obligation.
This is the mufta bihi position.
3
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
The phrase 'insha'Allah' in this context is customarily used for seeking barakah (blessing) or expressing reliance on Allah's will, not as a legal condition that suspends the obligation. The default in iqrar (confession) is that it is binding unless a genuine suspending condition is proven.
Hanafis rely on 'urf (custom) and the principle that utterances are interpreted according to common usage.
4
Note the cross-madhhab difference
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) may treat the phrase as a condition that suspends the confession until Allah wills, making the confession contingent. The Hanafi school rejects this interpretation.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf; the Hanafi view is based on the stronger evidence of custom.
5
Apply to practice
In a court, if a person confesses with 'insha'Allah', the judge will uphold the confession and order payment. The creditor can claim the debt immediately.
The ruling applies to all confessions of rights (huquq), including debts and liabilities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن أقر ووَصَلَ إن شاء الله [ 1 ] قوله : ومَن أقر ... الخ؛ يعني مَن أقر بحق وقال : إن شاء الله تعالى متصلاً
And whoever confesses and connects 'insha'Allah' (if Allah wills) ... [1] His saying: 'Whoever confesses ... etc.' means whoever confesses a right and says 'if Allah wills' consecutively.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This is a ruling statement introducing the effect of saying 'inshā'Allāh' (if Allah wills) in a confession. The commentary explains that if a person confesses a right (e.g., a debt) and immediately says 'inshā'Allāh', the confession is not suspended; it is valid and binding because the phrase does not negate or condition the confession in a way that removes liability. The Hanafi view is that such a qualification does not prevent the confession from taking effect, as the phrase is often used for seeking blessing, not as a condition. The full ruling would discuss whether the phrase affects the confession’s validity or whether it is considered a conditional statement that suspends the obligation. Due to the incomplete text, the precise details are not fully available.

Key Terms
إن شاء الله (inshā' Allāh): A phrase meaning 'if Allah wills', used as a qualifier in utterances.
أقر (aqarra): He confessed, admitted a right or debt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The confession is invalid because of the condition.
B) The confession is valid and the debt is owed.
C) The confession is suspended until Allah wills.
D) The confession is considered a promise, not a binding admission.

Key Takeaway
Saying 'insha'Allah' does not invalidate a confession; the debt is still owed.

Exception in Acknowledgement: When the Excepted Item Differs in Genus
Commentary on exception ruling and inter-madhhab dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on exception in acknowledgement when the excepted item is of a different genus, explain the Hanafi proof, and compare it with the Shafi'i/Maliki position, identifying the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Exception in acknowledgement is valid only if the excepted item is of the same genus; otherwise the full debt is due.

When a person acknowledges a debt and adds an exception, the validity of that exception depends on the nature of the excepted item. The Hanafi school holds a strict condition: the exception must be of the same genus as the acknowledged item. This lesson examines the reasoning behind this rule and the inter-madhhab dispute with the Shafi'i and Maliki schools, which allow deduction by value even for different genera.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling: exception in acknowledgement is valid only if the excepted item is of the same genus as the acknowledged item. If different, the exception is void and the full acknowledged amount is due.
2
Identify the opposing view
Al-Shafi'i and Malik hold that exception is valid even if the excepted item is of a different genus, because the exception functions as a contradiction (mu'arada) that negates the ruling for the excepted item, and its value can be subtracted.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
The opponent argues that exception prevents the establishment of the ruling for the excepted item due to a contradicting evidence. Since the excepted item is of a different genus, its value is deducted from the acknowledged amount, acting upon the contradiction as much as possible.
This is an argument from the nature of exception as a form of contradiction.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi refutation has four parts: (1) Contradiction requires the same subject (mahall); here the subjects differ. (2) Acknowledgement is a binding report; one cannot later negate part of it. (3) If exception were a contradiction, partial and full contradiction would be equal, which is not the case. (4) The Quranic verse (al-Ankabut 29:14) shows exception is clarification, not contradiction.
The verse 'a thousand years less fifty years' means precisely 950 years, not a contradiction between two statements.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi – full debt is due; Shafi'i/Maliki – the value of the excepted item is deducted. For example, acknowledging 100 dirhams except a cloth: Hanafi says 100 dirhams due; Shafi'i/Maliki says 100 dirhams minus the cloth's value.
The mufta bihi position is the Hanafi view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بأعيانهما ثمن بأوصافهما ، حتى لو عينا تعلق العقد بأعيانهما. ولو وصفا ولم يُعيّنا صارَ حكمها كحكم الثمنين ؛ ولهذا يستوي الجيد والرديء فيهما ، فكانت في حكم الثبوت في الذمَّةِ كجنس واحد معنى، فالاستثناء تكلم بالباقي معنى لا صورة ، بخلاف غيرهما من الثوب وغيره، فإنّه مثلاً ليس جنس المقدرات معني ؛ لأنه لا يصلح ثمناً ، فلم يكن استثناؤه استخراجاً لا صورة ولا معنى، فكان باطلا معنى. وقال الشافعي : صح هذا الاستثناء، وبه قال مالك له ؛ لأنَّ حكم الاستثناء امتناع ثبوت الحكم في المستثنى ؛ لقيام الدليل المعارض، فإذا قال: له علي عشرة إلا خمسة، فكأنه قال : إلا خمسة فإنّها ليست علي، فإذا كان بطريق المعارضة من جنسه يجب إخراج قدره، وإن كان من خلاف جنسه يجب إخراج قيمته عملا بالدليل المعارض بقدر الإمكان. والجواب : إنَّ المعارضة لا تثبتُ عند اختلافِ المحلّ؛ لأنَّ انتفاء أحدهما لا ينافي ثبوت الآخر، فلا يتعارضان وأيضاً : إنَّ العبد لا يقدر على أن ينفي ما عليه من الواجب بطريق المعارضة، فإنّه إذا أقرَّ به لزمه ، ولا يتصور أن ينتفي بعد ذلك بإنكاره ، ولو كان بطريق المعارضة كما ذكره ؛ لاستوى فيه البعض والكل كما كالنسخ والاتصال والانفصال ؛ لأنه لا يشترط في المعارض أن يكون مقارناً ، وإنما ذلك في المغير. وأيضاً : الإقرار خبر، فلو كان بطريق المعارضة لكان أحدهما كذباً، وذلك لا يجوز؛ لكونه موجوداً في القرآن المجيد، حيث قال عز من قال : فَلَبِثَ فِيهِمْ أَلْفَ سَنَةٍ إِلَّا خمسين عاما (١) ، والمراد به أنه لبث فيهم تسعمئة وخمسين عاما.
With their specific identities as price with their descriptions. So if they are specified, the contract attaches to their specific identities. And if they are described without being specified, their ruling becomes like the ruling of two prices; hence the good and the bad are equal in them, so they are, in the ruling of being established in the dhimma, like one genus in meaning. Thus the exception [with 'in sha Allah'] is a speech about the remainder in meaning not in form, unlike other items like cloth and others, because that is not a genus of measured items in meaning, since it cannot serve as a price. Therefore, its exception is not an extraction neither in form nor in meaning, so it is void in meaning. Al-Shafi'i said: This exception is valid, and Malik agreed with him, because the ruling of exception is the prevention of establishing the ruling in the excepted item due to a contradicting evidence. So if he says: 'I owe him ten except five,' it is as if he said: 'except five which are not owed by me.' So if it is by way of contradiction from its genus, its amount must be excluded, and if it is from a different genus, its value must be excluded, acting upon the contradicting evidence as much as possible. The answer: Contradiction is not established when the subject differs, because the negation of one does not negate the existence of the other, so they do not contradict. Also, a slave cannot negate what is obligatory upon him by way of contradiction, because if he acknowledges it, it becomes binding, and it is inconceivable that it would be negated thereafter by his denial. And if it were by way of contradiction as he mentioned, then partial and full [contradiction] would be equal, like abrogation, conjunction, and disjunction, because it is not required in the contradictor to be concurrent; that is only in the modifier. Also, acknowledgement is a report, so if it were by way of contradiction, one of them would be a lie, and that is not permissible, because it is found in the Noble Quran where the Almighty said: 'So he remained among them a thousand years less fifty years' (al-Ankabut:14), meaning he remained among them nine hundred and fifty years.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the validity of exception in acknowledgement when the excepted item is of a different genus than the acknowledged item. The Hanafi position, as explained by the commentator, is that exception is valid only if the excepted item is of the same genus as the acknowledged item. Here, the discussion focuses on an acknowledgement where the item is described (like a debt in the dhimma) versus specified (like a specific item). The commentator explains that when a person acknowledges a debt described in general terms, the exception of a specific item like a cloth or house is invalid because that item is not of the same genus as the debt (which is measured in weight or volume). The Hanafis argue that the exception must be meaningful, meaning it must extract something of the same kind. Al-Shafi'i and Malik hold that exception is valid even if the excepted item is of a different genus, because the exception functions as a contradiction (mu'arada) that negates part of the acknowledged debt by value. The Hanafi response refutes this on several grounds: (1) contradiction requires the same subject (mahall), but here the acknowledged debt and the excepted item are different in nature, so no contradiction occurs. (2) In acknowledgement, once a person acknowledges a debt, he cannot later negate part of it by a mere statement; acknowledgement is a binding report. (3) If exception were a form of contradiction, it would apply equally to parts and whole, which is not the case. (4) The Quranic example (a thousand less fifty years) is cited to show that exception is not a contradiction but a clarification; the verse means exactly nine hundred and fifty years, not a contradiction between two statements. Thus, the Hanafi ruling stands: exception in acknowledgement is only valid when the excepted item is of the same genus and can be extracted in form and meaning from the acknowledged amount.

Key Terms
استثناء (istithna'): An exception made in an acknowledgement, where the acknowledger excludes something from the acknowledged item.
إقرار (iqrar): An acknowledgement of a right or debt against oneself.
معارضة (mu'arada): A legal contradiction where one evidence negates another; in this context, the opponent uses it to argue that exception negates part of the acknowledgement.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if someone acknowledges a debt of 100 dirhams and says 'except this cloth,' what is the ruling?
A) The exception is valid and the value of the cloth is deducted from the debt.
B) The exception is invalid and the full 100 dirhams are due.
C) The exception is valid only if the cloth is of the same genus as dirhams.
D) The acknowledgement itself is void because of the exception.

Key Takeaway
Exception in acknowledgement is valid in the Hanafi school only when the excepted item is of the same genus as the acknowledged item; otherwise the exception is void and the full amount is due.
